<span id="freeTextContainer13257501411126097962"><br/><br/>I loved this book! <br/>This is so beautifully written...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815677.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Blythe.. A girl so alone, Drowning in depression. What is her life? Nothing...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815678.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>"What I find interesting, at least from a human-interest standpoint, is that while I am painfully aware of my feelings and symptoms, I’m unable to shake them and move forward. I am stagnant, I guess. Which makes sense given that stagnant is sort of just a synonym for depressed ."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815679._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She's lost everything which mattered and its her fault? That's what she thinks. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815680.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Now 4 year</span>
  <span id="freeText13257501411126097962" style="display:none"><br><br>I loved this book! <br>This is so beautifully written...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815677.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Blythe.. A girl so alone, Drowning in depression. What is her life? Nothing...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815678.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"What I find interesting, at least from a human-interest standpoint, is that while I am painfully aware of my feelings and symptoms, I’m unable to shake them and move forward. I am stagnant, I guess. Which makes sense given that stagnant is sort of just a synonym for depressed ."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815679._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She's lost everything which mattered and its her fault? That's what she thinks. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413966ra/815680.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now 4 years later Blythe is still stuck in that rut she was in.<br>Until she meets a boy at a Lake...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815681.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Chris... <br>Never did Blythe know that in those moments this boy was going to save her from drowning in herself.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Feel me.” He inhales, and his chest presses into me. “Breathe,” he tells me. “Breathe with me.”</i>
</b><br><br>I loved Sabin, oh this boy is such a beautiful soul!!!!<br>And Estelle and every single one of this family.<br><br><b>"My secret wish to believe in fate, spirituality, or something so I don’t only have to exist with the cold certainty I feel that there is nothing bigger than random chance."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815682.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Blythe starts hanging with Chris and their family, she begins to feel alive...<br>Life has meaning...<br><br><b>

  <i>"You are the great love of my life that I’m never going to have.”</i>
</b><br><br>Random lyrics went through my head!! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815684.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413966i/815685._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Until its time to take the next step and fight for what she wanted! <br><br><b>"There is no set pattern to grief, despite what every stupid psych text has told me. There is no time frame that dictates when and how you’ll feel what you feel. <div id="review_618492591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618492591" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618492591?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=cry-baby-books">cry-baby-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618492591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4847320588026983199"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422035i/839226._SX540_.jpg' width='410' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jessica Park brilliantly wrote this novel and had me from the first couple of pages. I’m still wrapping my mind around the complete story, it was truly an experience. The writing was fantastic, the cast of characters were truly unique and the story… was so heartbreaking and uplifting that a full 5 Star rating and a standing ovation is warranted!<br/><br/><br/>I don’t think I’ll give a full description in this review but I’ll say that Sabin, Eric, Estelle and Christopher Shepard were absolutely fantastic. They </span>
  <span id="freeText4847320588026983199" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422035i/839226._SX540_.jpg" width="410" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jessica Park brilliantly wrote this novel and had me from the first couple of pages. I’m still wrapping my mind around the complete story, it was truly an experience. The writing was fantastic, the cast of characters were truly unique and the story… was so heartbreaking and uplifting that a full 5 Star rating and a standing ovation is warranted!<br><br><br>I don’t think I’ll give a full description in this review but I’ll say that Sabin, Eric, Estelle and Christopher Shepard were absolutely fantastic. They were loving, strong and broken. The strength and friendship that they gave Blythe to heal was incredible. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>“I am hit with the enormity of the impact that this family is having in my life. They, and mostly Chris, are saving me. Or teaching me to save myself.”</i>
</b><br><br><br>The love and connection that Blythe and Christopher shared could be called many things. Perhaps fate, however you define Blythe and Christopher they were connected, they were in love and their sex scenes STEAMY and you’ll be invested in them as much as I was. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>“He tastes like eternity, and healing, and completion. <br>No one else could ever kiss me like this, of that I am positive.<br>I could breathe him in forever.<br>I could fall in love forever.”</i>
</b><br><br><br>I have to warn a reader that I was <b>pissed</b> and I mean pissed about some actions on Christopher’s part. I mean probably as much or more than Blythe. <br><br><b>
  <i>“You are the greatest love of my life that I’m never going to have.”</i>
</b><br><br>Blythe doesn’t crumble but stands strong through it all. <br><br>I would love for Jessica Park’s to give us a chapter in Christopher’s pov --- <b>Pretty Please!!</b>-- because even though his actions were explained I wanted more on the subject.<br><br><br>When it’s all said and done, I get the whys, the reveals and I absolutely loved how the group comes together again. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>“I love you simply because I do. And that’s it.”</i>
</b><br><br> <br>Truthfully, all roads and events tied Blythe to the Shepard clan. Through their saving and support she was able to be strong enough to save Christopher and in turn, complete a circle of support and healing for all characters. <br><br>Truly a magnificent weaved tale (although I guessed at some of their connection) the end result is nonetheless a true MASTERPIECE!!! <br><br><b>
  <i>“What are you doing?"<br><br>"Loving you," he says simply. "If you'll let me."<br><br>"Always. God, always.”</i>
</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4847320588026983199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_543875637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543875637" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543875637?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543875637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13133606203609361962"><br/><b>Left Drowning</b> started off harmlessly enough and then ripped through <b>
  <i>ALL</i>
</b> of my emotions, bringing me to soaring heights only to crash me down to earth shattering lows!! Jessica Park thankfully left me on a blissful high. Ms. Park, you have done a number on me, and I’m still recovering from the roller coaster ride my heart and mind rode!! <br/><br/>When we first meet Blythe, she’s not putting her best foot forward. She’s coming home, after some college party, in a drunken stupor and barely makes it into</span>
  <span id="freeText13133606203609361962" style="display:none"><br /><b>Left Drowning</b> started off harmlessly enough and then ripped through <b>
  <i>ALL</i>
</b> of my emotions, bringing me to soaring heights only to crash me down to earth shattering lows!! Jessica Park thankfully left me on a blissful high. Ms. Park, you have done a number on me, and I’m still recovering from the roller coaster ride my heart and mind rode!! <br /><br />When we first meet Blythe, she’s not putting her best foot forward. She’s coming home, after some college party, in a drunken stupor and barely makes it into her dorm room. She’s been drifting along like this for much of her college years, numb to everything around her. Blythe hasn’t dealt with her past and so it still cripples her. But then a change starts to take place when she meets a brood of siblings, quirky, loud, and lovable, and she starts to slowly come out of her fog. There’s Estelle and Eric, the twins, and Sabin the outgoing, flirt, and then there’s Chris, the oldest sibling and thief of Blythe’s heart. <br /> <br />Chris feels safe and in control to Blythe and so she starts to reconcile her past a little more and more with his support. The brothers and sisters help as well, and Blythe the connection she makes with each of them heals her just a little more. With every passing day, though, Blythe is falling harder and harder for Chris, even with his warnings that she’s too good for him, she’s <i>too</i> much for him, and more than he can take. <br /><br />On closer inspection it becomes apparent that the siblings are not the perfect fun loving group shown to the outside. Blythe knows a dark cloud hangs over them but doesn’t push. She knows the need for privacy and the desire to pretend everything is okay can be necessary to survive. She hopes that the connection she shares with Chris will turn into something more when they both can handle it. She’s willing to wait for it, it’s everything to her.<br /><br />Like I said in the beginning, Jessica Park took me on one hell of a roller coaster ride. I was climbing up a slow hill creaking along, getting higher and higher, my heart and hopes in a crescendo at the top. Happy, happy, joy, joy, wonderful highs!! Delicious, steamy, OH-MY-STARS-STEAMY-SCENES!! Then without warning I’m crashing down the other side down, heart dumped somewhere at the bottom. I <i>CRIED</i> angry tears, sad tears, and I was generally sort of raging for a good 20% of this book! My poor husband. Even a couple of my friends were not spared and got some ranty texts from me. There may or may not have been cursing involved (there was, lots of words beginning with the letter F!!!). I didn’t know if I could forgive or forget. But then the miracle that is Jessica Park’s writing, she turned it all around. I got answers, and reasons, and I’m <i>almost</i> ashamed at how much I wanted to murder a certain character knowing what I now know. My heart breaks for everything that was endured and so I can forgive, and I understand. Plus, things were not all that they seemed….<br /><br />I loved the final revelations, and how Ms. Park brilliantly put this whole story together. I figured out a few things in the beginning, but didn’t have the full scope until the end. I’m still <i>so</i> emotional and so affected from this read, my feelings are still <i>very</i> much at the surface, but I completely LOVED it!! I’ve been a big fan of Jessica Park since Flat-Out Love, and she did not disappoint with Left Drowning! <br /><br /><i>A copy was provided by Skyscape through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</i><br /><br />You can read this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/07/review-left-drowning-by-jessica-park.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13133606203609361962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1818979250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1818979250" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1818979250?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818979250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7580667878743078216"><b>1 Star</b><br/><br/><b>Really good sex ≠ a cure for mental illness</b><br/><br/>This book follows Blythe, who is still reeling from the loss of her parents. She spends her nights getting drunk and numbly moving through existence. In the first chapter she says:<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “So continues my endless search for physical feeling, sensation. Anything.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>She spends her days not wanting to get out of bed to so much as wash her hair, spending hours after hours mourning, and continuing to drink almost every night. <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “Not that I would classify m</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText7580667878743078216" style="display:none"><b>1 Star</b><br /><br /><b>Really good sex ≠ a cure for mental illness</b><br /><br />This book follows Blythe, who is still reeling from the loss of her parents. She spends her nights getting drunk and numbly moving through existence. In the first chapter she says:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “So continues my endless search for physical feeling, sensation. Anything.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />She spends her days not wanting to get out of bed to so much as wash her hair, spending hours after hours mourning, and continuing to drink almost every night. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Not that I would classify myself as depressed. Sure, I have numerous depressive symptoms, but I think that I have a good reason… I think back to my psych textbook and grimace as I think how clearly my symptoms match up to the clinical definition. Fine, fine. I’m depressed. There, I said it.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Depression is a real illness that impacts thousands of people each day. I’m not discounting these experiences or emotions. What I am discounting is the way the book chooses to address this. Blythe's only response is to go for a walk. <br /><br />But of course on this walk she meets not one… but <i>two</i> interesting and mysterious men who are immediately entranced by her. <br /><br />The first man bumps into her after grabbing coffee: <i>
  <blockquote> “Aren’t you going to ask me why I haven’t gone to bed yet? Given our close relationship, I’d think that my whereabouts would be an extremely pressing issue here. Your curiously should be driving you insane. Was Sabin at an all-night karaoke amusement park? Was he abducted by alien cowboy ghosts?</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Nobody talks like this to people THEY JUST MET.</b><br /><br />The second man is a chiseled Adonis who is skipping rocks down by the lack and she happens to swing by so of course he offers to show her how to skip rocks. And OF COURSE she’s suddenly really good at it. And turns to him:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> For no discernible reason, it feels unfathomable not to tell him. “My parents are dead.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Nobody talks like this to people THEY JUST MET.</b><br /><br />Unloading your trauma on a stranger you find attractive is not an interesting meet-cute. Instead of recognizing that Blythe is really struggling and maybe helping her find some help, hot guy (Chris) is like “ya know what, I’m pretty angsty I can roll with this, lets get lunch.”<br /><br />And during this lunch we learn <b>both strangers are brothers!</b> And naturally there’s a whole big family who loves Blythe and it’s insta friendship for everyone and they hang out all the time and braid each other’s hair. <br /><br />And all this interaction includes Chris being insufferable and Blythe somehow thinking it’s sooooo charming.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “So, I guess that it’s fucking cream of turnip soup, cabbage, and soda bread for you two.”<br />“Seriously, Estelle, enough with the swearing. I can cuss up a storm, but you’re my little sister and I can’t take it.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />(Oh fuck the fuck off, Chris. Your sister is a fucking adult and can say whatever the fuck she wants.)<br /><br />Chris and Blythe continue to bond over trauma and being edgy and say things like:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “There is no God. Not for us.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Blythe’s reaction to all of Chris’ angst and their burgeoning friendship is <b>to make Chris her central deity and also masturbate a lot.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “…are punishment for masturbating. For masturbating a lot. I think that I may have an addiction. A sex maniac beast has awoke and I am a horny mess nearly all the time.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Every time that he laughs at a line from the play or mutters to himself—or for Christ’s sake, sniffs—I practically shudder with lust.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Chris and I are inextricably connected Do I have factual reasons to know this? Proof? Assurances? No. None.</blockquote>
</i><br /><i>
  <blockquote> "Some people believe in God; I believe in Chris.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />THIS IS NOT HEALTHY<br /><br />A whole bunch of drama starts happening. Like they have sex and then Chris gets engaged to someone else and it was all very angsty for the sake of being angsty. <b>But the worst part was Blythe acting like Chris and his amazing sex gave her a reason to live.</b><br /><br />There’s a whole predictable twist about how their lives are interwoven and it’s fate and yadda yadda. But Blythe never works on herself or deals with anything. She just has a lot of sex and pining for Chris and decides <i>that’s</i> what living is. <br /><br />Again, the day Blythe realizes she is clinically depressed is the day she meets Chris. She never undergoes any treatment nor does anyone reach out to help. The only thing that changes is she meets Christ. But from that day on she was magically ‘better’ (or as she puts it “happy again.")<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion:</b><br /><br />Ew.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7580667878743078216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11394156973273891234"><br/><b> WHAT HAPPENED TO ME AFTER READING THIS BOOK </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/Need-a-Drink.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow%202/tumblr_m7sxrbOddH1qca88y.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430732ra/863685.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_m7sxrbOddH1qca88y.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/tumblr_m8roo8otsH1qhk6l1havealotoffeelings_zps9c38c785.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>This book was simply deep, ugly crying, and breathtakingly emotional. I was a utter and total wreck. Bought all my emotions out for good and even horrible reasons. I was so pulled into this story emotionally and mentally it felt like my own heart was breaking, it was ripped out, stamped out, stabbed a few times and tossed in the trash. <br/><br/><a href='http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/tumblr_mbfqwuZ8yU1rnhv55.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423955ra/844988.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mbfqwuZ8yU1rnhv55.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>My first book of Jessica Park and it's blew me away!! This author is def one of my favourites. <br/><b> 5++++</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11394156973273891234" style="display:none"><br><b> WHAT HAPPENED TO ME AFTER READING THIS BOOK </b><br><br><a href="http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/Need-a-Drink.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430732ra/863685.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m7sxrbOddH1qca88y.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/tumblr_m8roo8otsH1qhk6l1havealotoffeelings_zps9c38c785.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>This book was simply deep, ugly crying, and breathtakingly emotional. I was a utter and total wreck. Bought all my emotions out for good and even horrible reasons. I was so pulled into this story emotionally and mentally it felt like my own heart was breaking, it was ripped out, stamped out, stabbed a few times and tossed in the trash. <br><br><a href="http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/tumblr_mbfqwuZ8yU1rnhv55.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423955ra/844988.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mbfqwuZ8yU1rnhv55.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My first book of Jessica Park and it's blew me away!! This author is def one of my favourites. <br><b> 5+++++ STELLAR STARS </b><br><br><a href="http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow%202/cHSqp.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430732ra/863687.gif" alt=" photo cHSqp.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book gave me everything from total elation to absolute heartbreak and everything in between. Left Drowning is a powerful story of how shattering events in the past connect with the present and the future. How it haunts and drowns itself .The key is not to forget, not to accept, not always to forgive in order to move on...but to breathe. To find strength in others and to build a foundation based on love and trust in order to survive. <br><br><a href="http://s799.photobucket.com/user/79twilightlover/media/Bow-chicka-wow-wow/tumblr_mgxufo5bNV1rnlmxho1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_657824915" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/657824915" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/657824915?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18053912-left-drowning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=emotional-angsty-books">emotional-angsty-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657824915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15812744864695168183">4.5 ★'s<br/><br/>Blythe has never recovered from a traumatic event that killed her parents and permanently injured her brother four years ago. She carries all the guilt on her shoulders and she can barely keep her head above water. That is, until the day she meets two of the Shepherd brothers, each affecting her in ways she could never imagine, and allowing her to breathe once again.<br/><br/>To start off, I'd just like to say that I wasn't sure I wanted to read this book. First, the title is a bit daunting and eve</span>
  <span id="freeText15812744864695168183" style="display:none">4.5 ★'s<br><br>Blythe has never recovered from a traumatic event that killed her parents and permanently injured her brother four years ago. She carries all the guilt on her shoulders and she can barely keep her head above water. That is, until the day she meets two of the Shepherd brothers, each affecting her in ways she could never imagine, and allowing her to breathe once again.<br><br>To start off, I'd just like to say that I wasn't sure I wanted to read this book. First, the title is a bit daunting and even though, yes, the story is dark, the title is just a metaphor. Second, I've read the Flat-Out series and while good, I just wasn't sure I was interested in more of the same. Thankfully, this book is much, much better. While the Flat-Out series was more of the minor leagues, Jessica Park has seriously stepped up into the major leagues with this book. Yep, it's <i>that</i> good! <br><br>It was a bit crazy reading how damaged Blythe was and it takes a bit to get her full story. The interesting part is that we get all these clues and pieces of the puzzle as we go along. The fun part is trying to figure out how everything will fit together. And I love how Jessica Park did that! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/625086.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was a little disconcerting at how quickly and somewhat easily, Blythe came out of her "brokenness". That's not to say that she didn't struggle but she never had any setbacks and for the most part everything worked out. The only real problem was her dependence on Chris. She did talk a good talk though...and she almost made us...and herself believe all that stuff she was spewing. But who was she kidding? Still, it was fantastic seeing how everything developed and evolved. <br><br>Chris is an interesting character and probably even more broken than Blythe. You get that feel right from the beginning but his story takes even longer to get to. His feelings for Blythe seem true but then some drama happens...I would have loved his POV at that point. <br><br>The rest of the Shepherd clan are just as wonderful. Sabin was my favorite but you just knew what kind of trouble he was coming up against. I did love his relationship with "B". Estelle...again, you could see the trouble she was in but I loved her "sisterhood" with Blythe and how she was so giving. I will never forget "Neon Jesus". Eric seemed to be the one with his head screwed on right but there just couldn't be one to come out unfazed. I was happy with his relationship with Zach because it was nice having one normal person. <br><br>James is Blythe's brother and he has his own problems. His relationship with Blythe is not good in the beginning but as she gets better, so does things between them. It was wonderful seeing them work towards getting their relationship back to where it was and even better. <br><br>And I love Jonah! <br><br>Another problem was both these families have a ton of money...it makes things very convenient even if it is understandable as to why. It would have been more real - or relatable to have them not have things so easily. <br><br>And WOW was I surprised at the steamy scenes! I am very impressed with JP because as you know (or may not), there are no steamy scenes in Flat-Out Love. Now, Flat-Out Matt does have a bit but still I was not prepared. And I loved every minute...<i>and</i> I'm quite jealous! Yet again, it bothered me that it wasn't quite realistic. I know, I know...it's a fictional story but still. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/552460.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The drama between Chris and Blythe totally took me by surprise! I did not see that coming and I was shocked at how long it lasted! WTH? But I also loved it because I eat up all that emotional drama! However, it was a bit of a letdown at how easily (again) it was resolved. <br><br>The last twenty percent is action packed and we finally get all our answers. I did love the way we were filled in with how everyone was doing as Blythe did her marathon. I loved how they were there for each other! <br><br>So, a few minor complaints but overall, I really enjoyed the story. The "connections" between Chris and Blythe were well thought out and I loved how JP put them all together. (The urchin = brilliant!) <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380222758i/610356.gif" width="400" height="050" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Favorite quotes:<br><br>♥ "My shirt … found a new home.”<br><br>♦ "You are safe, sweet girl."<br><br>♥ “Being with you let me feel, feel <i>everything</i>, and I needed that. I remembered better with you, I healed better with you, and you made … you made everything real.”<br><br>♥ “You are the great love of my life that I’m never going to have.”<br><br>♥ “We’re like … puzzle pieces that fit together.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="15812744864695168183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_688623468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688623468" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1744269-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336067184p2/1744269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/688623468?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/1744269-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1744269-susan?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688623468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5021532716095337427">After this paragraph, this is a super-spoiling recap review. Sorry about that. I entirely agree with the New York Times critic A.O. Scott about <a href='http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/movies/films-dispense-with-storytelling-conventions.html?pagewanted=all' rel='nofollow noopener'>genre stories</a> and <a href='http://movies.nytimes.com/2013/06/07/movies/much-ado-about-nothing-directed-by-joss-whedon.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>knowing the ending</a> in advance. If a contemporary erotic late young adult novel is your type of book, you’ll like it no matter how much you hear from me ahead of reading it. As for me, the more frustrated I get while reading a book, the more I feel like telling you what crazy things happen in the story. Today I'm also in a life lesson mo</span>
  <span id="freeText5021532716095337427" style="display:none">After this paragraph, this is a super-spoiling recap review. Sorry about that. I entirely agree with the New York Times critic A.O. Scott about <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/movies/films-dispense-with-storytelling-conventions.html?pagewanted=all" rel="nofollow noopener">genre stories</a> and <a href="http://movies.nytimes.com/2013/06/07/movies/much-ado-about-nothing-directed-by-joss-whedon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">knowing the ending</a> in advance. If a contemporary erotic late young adult novel is your type of book, you’ll like it no matter how much you hear from me ahead of reading it. As for me, the more frustrated I get while reading a book, the more I feel like telling you what crazy things happen in the story. Today I'm also in a life lesson mood.<br /><br />Senior year of college is beginning, and Blythe realizes that she has been in a depressive and alcohol-fueled fog for the last four years, ever since her parents died in a house fire. Waking up one day, she decides to spend 24 hours without any booze, and within that time she independently meets Sabin, a junior who steals her coffee and decides in that second that they will be besties, and Chris, a senior who is built and can skip rocks. To make matters better, Sabin and Chris happen to be brothers, and their twin younger siblings go to the college too, and LOVE Blythe right away.<br /><br /><i>Romance book life lesson: when you think you are out of shape, wretched-looking and unused to social interaction, people will FALL IN LOVE WITH YOU. Also, when you make friends, make sure they come from the same family. Diversifying your friend group is needlessly complicated.</i><br /><br />In Blythe’s relief about being sober, meeting friendly people, and having a sweet crying session that doesn’t weird anyone out, she starts to go running to deal with her flabby yet bony legs. (<i>Life lesson: do not be content with being thin because EWWW celluloid.</i>) Blythe has had no focus for however many years, but now she is ready to do a 45-minute run her first time out. As anyone who has ever exercised before may predict, she gets tired and does the normal thing of rushing to her brand new friend, Chris, to complain about her physical unfitness and her family problems. Chris can’t solve the aunt issue (although he is a great listener and affirmer of Blythe’s feelings), but he can make Blythe a new playlist. Blythe thanks him by pulling him close for a sweaty kiss. Chris eventually pries her off and Blythe is MORTIFIED.<br /><br /><i>Life lesson: Complain to new acquaintances about things. It’s a huge turn on.</i><br /><br />Blythe avoids Chris for a little, even while she uses his playlist to get her through her full work-out. Things between the two get even more complicated when he shows up at her room one day to help her masturbate (Blythe’s second favorite thing to do after running). Meanwhile she continues to grow closer to Chris’s whole family. She even invites his little sister to move into her dorm room.<br /><br /><i>Life lesson: When you find the right guy, his whole family will adopt you as one of their own within weeks.</i><br /><br />As Blythe and the Shepherd siblings celebrate Thanksgiving together, Blythe begins to see that the Shepherd family is kind of dysfunctional after Sabin drunkenly tries to ride a cafeteria tray off a third floor roof. In Sabin’s belligerency he makes fun of his sister’s religious beliefs and his brother’s unwillingness to hook up with Blythe within a month of meeting her, and then Sabin thrusts his tongue down Blythe’s throat. Blythe forgives him because he’s so drunk he’s just not himself. The boy Shepherd twin and his boyfriend dampen Chris’s mattress while they’re waiting to see if Sabin falls off the roof.<br /><br /><i>Life lesson: Belligerent drunks shouldn’t be held to high standards. And don’t trust people not to mess up your mattress in a life-or-death situation when you’d expect them to be too worried to be hooking up.</i><br /><br />By Christmas, Blythe is doing great and starting to reconcile with her little brother (who has never followed the above life lesson, and has been pretty upset with Blythe for drunk dialing him at all hours). She and Chris manage to spend <del>forty pages</del> a week in bed together with no expectation of commitment. Blythe and Chris both realize they’re in love with each other, but that is too serious for Chris, who not only bails but gets engaged to the next girl he sees.<br /><br /><i>Life lesson: <del>Guys don’t buy the cow if they can get the milk for free?</del> Don’t date severely emotionally damaged guys.</i><br /><br />There is more than another third of the book after this point, and I will stop plot summarizing so as to avoid any more major spoilers.<br /><br />You may have guessed already that I was not swept away by this read. I had no wish to hang out with the Shepherd siblings (who sound horrible, taunting her for loving their brother, assaulting her drunk, and involving her in awkward sibling fights), and I stopped caring about Chris and Blythe in bed after her first orgasm (which doesn't even physically involve him). Credit to the author for making Blythe find herself before she settles down in a romance, and credit to her for mentioning a condom every few pages and sending characters with issues to therapy. Even with those credits, though, this left me dissatisfied and filling out a pretty harsh <a href="http://readthiseatthat.blogspot.com/2013/08/LeftDrowning.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Romance Rubric</a>.<br /><br /><i>Originally posted at <a href="http://readthiseatthat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Read This / Eat That</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5021532716095337427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_565153883" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/565153883" />
    <a title="Tessa Teevan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10602787-tessa-teevan"><img alt="Tessa Teevan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604514740p2/10602787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/565153883?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessa Teevan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessa Teevan" href="/user/show/10602787-tessa-teevan">Tessa Teevan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10602787-tessa-teevan?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10602787-tessa-teevan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10602787-tessa-teevan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer565153883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15543417021711833647">When we first meet Blythe McGuire, she's not living, she's barely existing at a small college in Wisconsin. Still grieving over the loss of her parents in a tragic fire four years ago, she shuts everyone out, spending her time going to class and drinking her nights away. She has an estranged relationship with her brother as she believes he blames her for the loss of their parents, so she is, on all accounts, alone. <br/><br/>Enter the Shepherd family. Y'all, if there's ever a fictional family that I want </span>
  <span id="freeText15543417021711833647" style="display:none">When we first meet Blythe McGuire, she's not living, she's barely existing at a small college in Wisconsin. Still grieving over the loss of her parents in a tragic fire four years ago, she shuts everyone out, spending her time going to class and drinking her nights away. She has an estranged relationship with her brother as she believes he blames her for the loss of their parents, so she is, on all accounts, alone. <br><br>Enter the Shepherd family. Y'all, if there's ever a fictional family that I want to be a part of, it's the Shepherds. The first Shepherd Blythe meets is Sabin, the flamboyant theatre major who helps draw Blythe out of her shell. In the same day, she meets his sexy older brother, Chris, and they fall into an easy friendship that soon turns to more. <br><br>Blythe and Chris are both jaded due to circumstances of their past. As Blythe begins to fall for Chris, it's evident that he feels the same, but it continuously resistant to pursue anything further than a friendship. He's so hot and cold that it's exhausting wondering which Chris is going to show up. <br><br>Can Blythe and Chris get over their tragic pasts in order to have a beautiful future, or has too much damage been done for them to overcome it in the name of love?<br>*****<br><b>Five stars are not enough for this book!</b><br>I finished Left Drowning three days ago and I am still literally at a loss as to what to say about this book. No words that I can type could ever give this book the justice that it deserves. This book resonated so deeply within my soul that I will never forget a single moment of it, and I don't want to. Jessica Park did an amazing job in bringing every emotion I could ever possibly feel to the surface. She took my heart, ripped it out of my chest, stomped on it, stabbed it, and tore it apart. When I didn't think it was possible, she repaired my heart in the most beautiful fashion and I finished this book with the cheesiest, largest grin that could ever grace my face, while crying tears of joy at the same time. Seriously. This. Book. Is. Incredible. <br><br>Blythe and Chris have undeniable chemistry that sizzles through the pages. The way that they are immediately drawn to each other is beautiful, as is the progression of their relationship. They truly are each other's saving graces. They're like puzzle pieces; they're meant solely for each other to create the perfect fit. I can't begin to form the words to express how much I love the relationship of Blythe and Chris. <br><br>At one point Chris utterly and totally destroys me and I was left wondering... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413982ra/815775.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Blythe's strength as she continued to heal was extremely admirable. She's now at the top of my list of favorite female heroines. I felt everything she did. I felt her pain, her sorrow, and her angst. I also felt her falling in love, her pain healing, and the familial love she felt for Sabin, Estella, Eric, and James. She may have been a zombie for the past four years, but with a little bit of help, she rejoined the land of the living, and I loved going on this journey with her. <br><br>I also need to give a special shout out to Sabin. He was probably the best secondary character that I've ever encountered in the literary world. He was just as important of a puzzle piece in putting Blythe back together again. He was the instigator, the push, the spark that she needed to begin living her life again. He was her person. And it was undeniably beautiful. <br><br>I read <b>Left Drowning</b> on my birthday, and I'm pretty sure I freaked my husband out. If there's ever a book to make you ugly cry, this one is it! After crying on the couch for over an hour, I made my husband go to the store and buy me a bottle of wine because my heart seriously needed some liquid courage to continue this story. Jessica Park's writing style is so effortless, and she writes in such a way that the characters pop off of the page and instantly grasp onto your heart. I connected with this book in a way that I haven't experienced in a very long time. <br><br>Don't let me scare you with my talks of all the crying and emotional wreck that I was while reading this book. This payoff is more than worth it in the end. If you take only one recommendation from me for the rest of my blogging life, Left Drowning needs to be your choice. I'll even mail you a gift package of Kleenex tissues and chocolate to help you cope. I'd send wine, but I'm not really good at sharing that. I'll even send a few free hugs your way. You're going to need them. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/592029.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amazing, heartbreaking, devastating, tear-inducing, beautiful story. <br><br><b>THANK YOU, NETGALLEY!!!!!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413982ra/815776.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15543417021711833647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_685902498" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/685902498" />
    <a title="Mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22667925-mia"><img alt="Mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406604077p2/22667925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/685902498?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia" href="/user/show/22667925-mia">Mia</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer685902498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14915474692976991017"><b>5 stars for an unbelievably beautiful story!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385413400i/7144259.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was my first Jessica Park book and I cannot believe how much I loved it! This story was so much more than just a book; It was a heart breaking journey of family, love, guilt, healing.<br/><br/><b>Meet Blythe McGuire.</b> 4 years ago, she experiences a tragedy that took away her loved ones, and since then she's been just a shell of the person she once was. She hasn't been living her life, she's just been surviving through it. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385935780ra/7262223.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She pushes away everyone and lives a lo</span>
  <span id="freeText14915474692976991017" style="display:none"><b>5 stars for an unbelievably beautiful story!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385413400i/7144259.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was my first Jessica Park book and I cannot believe how much I loved it! This story was so much more than just a book; It was a heart breaking journey of family, love, guilt, healing.<br><br><b>Meet Blythe McGuire.</b> 4 years ago, she experiences a tragedy that took away her loved ones, and since then she's been just a shell of the person she once was. She hasn't been living her life, she's just been surviving through it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385935780ra/7262223.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She pushes away everyone and lives a lonely life, relying on alcohol and pointless parties to get her through the guilt she carries with her. One day she meets <b>Christopher Shepard,</b> and some how they just <b>connect.</b> They make each other feel again, in all the best and worst ways.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385413400i/7144261._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Something strong draws them together that neither of them can place, but neither is ready for a relationship. They can't deny the bond they share as they grow closer and closer together. Along with Chris, Blythe befriends Sabin, his younger brother. Before she knows it, she finds herself a part of the Shepard clan and after so long of being alone, Blythe has found a place she belongs. <br><br>Now, I have never liked the idea of insta-love in books. It just feels unrealistic to me. I wouldn't say Chris and Blythe had insta-love or insta-lust, it was more like... <b>
  <i>Insta-emotional-connetion.</i>
</b> Sounds a little weird, right? I was more than a little skeptical at first, but the way their relationship progressed and you saw the way they grew to love each other was so captivating and emotional. It was realistic. You could feel their bond, their chemistry. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385413400i/7144262._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although they connected so fast, their relationship was still slow burn and riveting. Chris, oh Chris. He made me swoon, cry, he broke my heart and destroyed me. I wanted to shake him at times, but nothing the characters did was out of reason. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385935780ra/7262224.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For so long, just like Blythe, Chris has lived in the darkness of his past, but unlike Blythe, he pretends. Strong, protective, he never puts down the mask. He fights for those he cares about -his siblings. But for the first time, he is forced to feel again. Blythe makes him feel everything he's spent so long shutting down, and it scares him shitless. He pushes her away, but eventually they find their way back and overcome their demons together. As the pieces of their tragic past begin to unravel, my heart broke for them in every way.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385413400i/7144260._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The characters were incredible! I loved loved loved Estella, Eric, Zach, Sabin, James. Each and every one of the characters, no matter how small the role, was written with so much dept that I felt so connected and invested in each one of their stories. All of them had their own demons they struggled with, and my heart broke for each and every one. <br><br>Just hearing the plot may sound likes its done so many times before –the girl with PTSD meets the boy who changes her life. But it's not. The way it was written so eloquently and beautifully, with so much emotion puts this book in a shelf of and in itself. I can't think of one book that could be compared to this one because it was such a special story.<br><br>And, I was pleasantly surprised by the steam in this book! It was <b>HOT</b>! Holy crap, does Jessica Park know how to write a sex scene or what!<br><br>I wish there were words express how much I adored this book. This was my first Jessica Park book and I am so excited to read more from her! This book was entertaining, emotional and I had tears all the way through but I loved every page. <i>Left Drowning</i> has found a permanent place on my favorite shelf and I look forward to reading it again and again!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We’ll make it to that finish line, won’t we, Blythe?” <br>“Always.”<i></i></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br></span>

<div id="review_620979950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/620979950" />
    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/620979950?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18053912-left-drowning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer620979950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3157520083529803708">For more reviews, visit - > <a href='http://www.jacquelinesreads.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jacqueline's Reads</a> <br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/tEXfzAH' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840359._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>4.5 fully submerged Stars!</b><br/><br/><b><i>Left Drowning</i> not only has a beautiful, title and cover, but an emotionally gripping story of intense love.</b><br/><br/><i>Left Drowning</i> is nothing like Jessica Park’s last book I’ve read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544734938' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flat-out Love</a> and it just amazes me! Sure, the title <i>Left Drowning</i> is a little depressing, but I seriously thought I was going into something light and fluffy and boy was I in for a shock! <b>BUT A GOOD SHOCK</b> Oh <i>Left Drowning</i> is very steamy … yeah I know</span>
  <span id="freeText3157520083529803708" style="display:none">For more reviews, visit - &gt; <a href="http://www.jacquelinesreads.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline's Reads</a> <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/tEXfzAH" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840359._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4.5 fully submerged Stars!</b><br><br><b><i>Left Drowning</i> not only has a beautiful, title and cover, but an emotionally gripping story of intense love.</b><br><br><i>Left Drowning</i> is nothing like Jessica Park’s last book I’ve read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544734938" rel="nofollow noopener">Flat-out Love</a> and it just amazes me! Sure, the title <i>Left Drowning</i> is a little depressing, but I seriously thought I was going into something light and fluffy and boy was I in for a shock! <b>BUT A GOOD SHOCK</b> Oh <i>Left Drowning</i> is very steamy … yeah I know you wanted to know that too.<br><br><b>[Disclaimer]</b><br><br>I got to put the disclaimer because I really need to stress that <i>Left Drowning</i> isn’t anything like <i>Flat-Out Love</i>. <i>Left Drowning</i> is ten times more emotional and basically you are in for a roller-coaster ride of highs and lows. If you like this kind of read (which I do!) then proceed.<br><br><b>[Summary]</b><br><br> Blythe is entering her senior year in college and first off, we notice something is seriously making Blythe unhappy and upset, we just don’t know why. One day she meets Chris at a secluded river and instantly forms a connection with him. Both Blythe and Chris have past issues and as they try to overcome disturbing histories, it either strengthens their relationship or pushes them apart.<br><br><b>Blythe</b><br><br>The beginning is a bit descriptive and usually this irritates me because I do not like descriptive writing, I know, to-each-their-own, BUT this time, it worked for me. Why? Well, it’s all about character build-up. I really got to know Blythe in the first few chapters. I got into the raw and gritty side of her and it was very refreshing. I also liked her sense of humor.<br><br><b>
  <i> No one else could ever kiss me like this, of that I am positive. I could breathe him in forever. I could fall in love forever.</i>
</b><br><br><b>Chris</b><br><br>Oh lord, what can I say about Chris? I am up and down with him. Sometimes I want to punch him in the face and sometimes I want to rip his clothes off and lick his abs. Chris is what I call a flawed Hero. He isn’t perfect, but somehow he balances Blythe. And when Chris said <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Being with you let me feel, feel everything, and I needed that. I remembered better with you, I healed better with you, and you made… you made everything real <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>… I just fainted. Major SWOON right?!<br><br><b>Overall</b><br><br><b>I want to point out a few things that are worth mentioning.<br><br>♥ I was grabbed right from the beginning!<br><br>♥ Chris and Blythe’s emotional past issues were not only shocking, but very moving.<br><br>♥ <i>Left Drowning</i> was one ball of emotional tension!<br><br>♥ Favorite scene… the shower scene! </b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/WT0DGFc" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840360.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>A few single words that just gutted me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ 1.) Sea urchin (I Know!!!), 2.) Matthew college shirt (I double know!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>… yeah it’s kind of like that.<br><br>I have to talk about the shower scene and no, I am not giving anything away people. It’s not a sex scene or anything like that. It’s just a moving and pivotal point in the read and it bumped up my rating. There are a few times when I read a powerful scene, I actually stop and think about it, this was one of them. WOW, is all I can say to that. <br><br>I LOVED the title reference. If you have read my past reviews, then you know that is the NUMBER ONE thing I look for in a read. I try to figure out why the author picked the title (if it’s not an obvious one) and Jessica Park … damn girl, you know how to write. When I got to the title reference I was like, <b>OH.MY.GOD… LOVE!</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/LxQ3hux" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840361.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Okay okay, so why didn’t I give this a 5 star rating? I usually don’t like to point out the negatives when I give a 4+ star review and I don’t really think this is a negative, I think it’s a personal preference, BUT I don’t want people to read my review and have certain expectations and then hate me, so I decided with my 4.5 star rating because I felt like Chris was just a bit too flawed for me. I know, I’m a dreamer and as much as I love flawed characters, I felt like Chris was too much one way.<br><br>However, I can’t stress enough the intensity of <i>Left Drowning</i> I know there are many readers that love damaged characters, tension filled romances and shocking situations, so if you are one of them, then I definitely recommend <i>Left Drowning</i>. If not for that, then because Jessica Park is one bad-a$$ writer and I wish her and I are best-friends.<br><br>
  <a href="http://imgur.com/Ne1U0eY" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840362.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/tE7VNb9" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422397i/840363.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>An ARC was provided in exchange for an honest review via Netgally</i><br><br>For more reviews, visit - &gt; <a href="http://www.jacquelinesreads.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline's Reads</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_621268924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621268924" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621268924?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=mature">mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=better-than-i-expected">better-than-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621268924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12353203737709877018"><b>Initial reaction:</b> This book had a lot of caveats to it with respect to elements that I think could've been presented better and fleshed out. I really didn't like the heroine much - whereas the surrounding cast of characters were a little more tolerable, and the fact that the ending came full circle bumped this up to a higher rating than I was initially going to give it.<br/><br/>This is probably going to be a solid 2.5 to 3 stars, depending on how I sort through how to explain what this novel did well and</span>
  <span id="freeText12353203737709877018" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> This book had a lot of caveats to it with respect to elements that I think could've been presented better and fleshed out. I really didn't like the heroine much - whereas the surrounding cast of characters were a little more tolerable, and the fact that the ending came full circle bumped this up to a higher rating than I was initially going to give it.<br /><br />This is probably going to be a solid 2.5 to 3 stars, depending on how I sort through how to explain what this novel did well and what it didn't.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />For a book I requested on accidental terms, I did not expect to be somewhat taken by Jessica Park's "Left Drowning." In the scheme of New Adult reads I've picked up as of late, this knocked many of its peer reads in the group in terms of plausible character development, conflict, real world tangibility, and connectivity.<br /><br />But I could argue it had several caveats that I outright didn't like, and I would say don't completely shed the coat of stereotyping that typifies this age group. There is some (male) slut shaming, the heroine is pretty unlikable in spurts (including one measure where she jokes about "sexually assaulting/molesting" her lover), and there are times when I'd like to say that the college environment could've been more vivid, but as far as the conflict and character dynamic were concerned - this was much more plausible than some of the other reads I've had thus far.<br /><br />I would give a warning about the strong sexual content that's in this book, and note it could easily fit under adult contemporary erotic romance. It personally didn't bother me (perhaps with exception for the repetitiveness and long, drawn out nature of such scenes - I've read better in the scheme of some writers), but I get that this is a read for anyone 18+. It is clearly NOT for children/YA.<br /><br />To take a brief tangent, I think one of the other reasons I liked this story so much is because it reminds me of a Sundance film I saw many years ago (whose name eludes me now). It was one of the titles I picked up back when I used to rent movies from Blockbuster (yes, it was a while ago) and the movie was under the heading Youth Restricted Viewing, or YRV. It was my freshman year of college when I watched it. The storyline revolved around a bunch of college friends who fell in and out of love in their relationships and dealt with a lot of tough subjects (including parental deaths, personal tragedies, growing pains) for the friends they highlighted, a group of three. It had strong sexual content, but none of it felt exploitative or for the sake of providing a conflict vehicle - it was just showing their lives and the conflict was contained in real world context with respect to things that directly impacted the relationships and personal lives of the characters in the story. It never felt that the conflict was thrown in willy-nilly.<br /><br />"Left Drowning" is evocative of that, telling the story of college senior Blythe McGuire. She's six months away from graduation, living her life in a fog of sorts. She starts off the novel drunk, depressed, and pretty much stuck in a rut, which I'll admit made me worry about where the story would go. Her parents are dead, her brother hates her for a tragedy that remains unspoken of until a good way into the novel (and by that time, I understood where her grief originated). She then meets rather odd personalities - first Sabin (whose over the top personality may make or break some readers) then Christopher (Chris). Chris actually has a nice introduction scene where he engages in a skipping stone lesson with Blythe, though there are some awkward moments of drama I felt that did eventually smooth themselves for the better in terms of the character development.<br /><br />I am happy to say that this book had absolutely no male characters (with the exception of an obvious antagonist) that were abusive jerks and glorified for the sake of that abuse. I was starting to think that every NA book I picked up would have a protagonist that I would either not care enough about to follow in the story or that I would absolutely loathe to the point of oblivion. The characters in this actually felt...normal. Flawed yes, problematic at times, yes, but ultimately - they were normal people dealing with some tough situations. Blythe actually comes to terms with meeting Chris and Sabin's family (they're brothers), and ultimately the story is kind of a coming to terms for Blythe in that she learns what it means to come outside of her grief and remember the things that hurt her.<br /><br />What kept this from being a higher rated read for me personally were some measures that I couldn't really look over as the story transpired. I felt that the narrative was a slow burner - sometimes it worked, sometimes it was a little dull and overly introspective. I also think the two shifts in POV (from predominantly first perspective to third) were awkward and may have been better if it had kept to one POV throughout the narrative. I've read some stories that toggled between the POV in a great way (see my thoughts on Sophie Hannah's "Little Face"), but this actually threw me out of the story when they came up and I didn't - at first - know what they were leading up to. I also wasn't really fond of the long passages of religious bargaining, though I understood where it was coming from and why - I just thought it took me out of the novel for frequency.<br /><br />I thought the vast majority of the characters in this novel were worth following, though Blythe got on my nerves more often than not. I had a hard time with her in turns of the story - though I think in the moments of her grief and coming to terms with certain things - I realized why she acted that way and could sympathize for the magnitude of the reveals. The dramatic elements were punctuated well in certain turns of the story (especially with respect to personal grief). I really wasn't expecting to be blindsided by a twist with respect to the relationships that came within 5% of the novel's end. I have to admit that was well done and I didn't see it coming.<br /><br />On the other hand, there were dramatic points that really weren't followed that well, including a point where Blythe suddenly forgives Chris of a pretty darned major transgression. Could I see that happening in real life? Sure. Do I think the coming to terms would be that quick? Absolutely not. Some of the interactions between characters - both intimate and casual interactions - were fluffy, but I actually handled that better than some of the awkward turns where the emotional recuperation time just didn't mesh.<br /><br />I'll admit the sex scenes and self pleasure scenes made this book longer than it should've been. I'm not knocking them for inclusion because they didn't feel exploitative and out of context with the novel, but I'm pretty sure that there was a good 10% of this novel that had nothing but one sex scene after the other. In some of the better erotic romance novels I've read, these are balanced with more anticipation, but in this some of them were repetitive and likely because they were in too close proximity.<br /><br />In the end, I think if I took this novel for what it had to offer, it was fine, and I was appreciative of the experience when it was all said and done. It's one of the better examples of developed storylines I've seen in NA. I would classify this more as adult contemporary erotic romance more, but I think I see the NA classification because it does invoke a college environment, it does invoke a proper coming to terms for the age range it's depicting, and it does carry its respective themes with some weight and maturity compared to the vast majority of stories I've perused here. It was worth the time and I think some might end up liking this more than I did.<br /><br />Overall score: 2.5/5<br /><br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher Amazon.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/66575688-whitney">Whitney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>
